  <meta content="Weston Residence" name="twitter:title"/>
  <meta content="The Weston Residence nestles in a valley adjacent to the Saugatuck River. In plan and section, the elements of the house engage the site in a way that purposefully blurs the transition and distinction between the built and natural environment.

As the house is approached from a road that begins high on a cliff above, the roofscape, or fifth facade, becomes a critical element of the design. Terraced planes planted with year-round, region-specific succulents step down the hill. Bedrooms project out into these roof gardens, giving a feeling of being fully immersed in the landscape. The planted roofs are also integral to the high-performance building envelope.

Interior and exterior spaces are joined through views, portals, and material ..." name="twitter:description"/>

              <div class="step edit" style="display:none">
              </div>
              <div class="step read">
               <div class="js-rendered-content">
                <div class="the-description js-the-description">
                 <span class="copy js-copy">
                  The Weston Residence nestles in a valley adjacent to the Saugatuck River. In plan and section, the elements of the house engage the site in a way that purposefully blurs the transition and distinction between the built and natural environment.
                  <br/>
                  <br/>
                  As the house is approached from a road that begins high on a cliff above, the roofscape, or fifth facade, becomes a critical element of the design. Terraced planes planted with year-round, region-specific succulents step down the hill. Bedrooms project out into these roof gardens, giving a feeling of being fully immersed in the landscape. The planted roofs are also integral to the high-performance building envelope.
                  <br/>
                  <br/>
                  Interior and exterior spaces are joined through views, portals, and material continuity. A glass-backed fireplace provides an elegant surprise. Like other glass houses, the landscape becomes the decoration for the rooms, playing with transparency during the day and reflectivity at night.
                  <br/>
                  <br/>
                  Photography: Taggart Sorensen
                 </span>
                </div>
                <script>
                 // temporary code for description toggle
        page.add_feature({
            require: ['jquery', 'globals'],
            callback: function(app, $, globals) {
                var $outer, $inner, orig_max_height, oldtxt, newtxt;

                $outer = $('#weston-residence-description .js-the-description');
                $inner = $outer.find('.js-copy');
                
                oldtxt = $outer.find('.js-copy').html();

                if (oldtxt) {
                    // clean description 
                    //newtxt = oldtxt.replace(/&lt;br\s*[\/]?&gt;/gi, ' ').replace('&nbsp;',' ');
                    //$outer.find('.js-copy').html(newtxt);

                    // see if description is too long and if so add click handler
                    orig_max_height = $outer.css('max-height').replace('px','');
                    globals.fn.once_visible($inner, function(){
                        if (orig_max_height &gt;= $inner.height() + 12) {
                            $outer.addClass('fully-visible');
                        } else {
                            $outer.click(function(){
                                if ($outer.data('open') === true) {
                                    $outer.css('max-height', '').removeClass('open').data('open', false);;
                                } else {
                                    $outer.css('max-height', $inner.height()).addClass('open').data('open', true);
                                }
                            });
                        }
                    });
                }
            }
        });
                </script>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>

&quot;type&quot;: &quot;hero&quot;, &quot;id&quot;: 941721}, &quot;name&quot;: &quot;Weston Residence&quot;, &quot;constr_status&quot;: &quot;built&quot;, &quot;building_size&quot;: &quot;&quot;, &quot;completion_date&quot;: &quot;2013-01-01T00:00:00&quot;, &quot;global_id&quot;: &quot;projects.project.139854&quot;, &quot;budget&quot;: -1.0, &quot;browse_hero&quot;: &quot;2014-10-02T09:25:00&quot;, &quot;browse_hero_in_feed&quot;: &quot;Thursday 09:25:00 - October 02, 2014&quot;, &quot;absolute_url&quot;: &quot;/projects/weston-residence/&quot;, &quot;pk&quot;: 139854, &quot;featured&quot;: 0, &quot;size&quot;: &quot;&quot;, &quot;verbose_name&quot;: &quot;Project&quot;, &quot;description&quot;: &quot;The Weston Residence nestles in a valley adjacent to the Saugatuck River. In plan and section, the elements of the house engage the site in a way that purposefully blurs the transition and distinction between the built and natural environment.\r\n\r\nAs the house is approached from a road that begins high on a cliff above, the roofscape, or fifth facade, becomes a critical element of the design. Terraced planes planted with year-round, region-specific succulents step down the hill. Bedrooms project out into these roof gardens, giving a feeling of being fully immersed in the landscape. The planted roofs are also integral to the high-performance building envelope.\r\n\r\nInterior and exterior spaces are joined through views, portals, and material continuity. A glass-backed fireplace provides an elegant surprise. Like other glass houses, the landscape becomes the decoration for the rooms, playing with transparency during the day and reflectivity at night.\r\n\r\nPhotography: Taggart Sorensen&quot;}, &quot;email&quot;: &quot;&quot;, &quot;related&quot;: {&quot;first_name&quot;: &quot;Louise&quot;, &quot;last_name&quot;: &quot;Harpman&quot;, &quot;hero&quot;: null, &quot;description&quot;: &quot;I have always maintained commitment to teaching as well as practice. I currently hold the position of Associate Professor in Architecture, Urban Design, and Sustainability at NYU's Gallatin School of Individualized Study. I have taught architecture at Yale, Penn, and the University of Texas at Austin, where I was also the Associate Dean for Undergraduate Programs.  In addition to our office projects and teaching, I serve as a competition adviser and juror, as well as an architectural adviser to universities, museums, and private individuals to assist them in selecting architects and landscape architects. \nI love the process of thinking and making, and the way that groups of people come together to create spaces and places.\n\nI am a member of the Board of Directors of Open House New York. I was the first Senior Fellow of the Design Trust for Public Space, on whose Board of Directors I also served. I am a member of the Architectural League of New York, the American Institute of Architects, the Municipal Art Society, and the New York Academy of Science.&quot;, &quot;created&quot;:    page.add_feature({
                require: [],
                callback: function(app) {
                    var init_addthis = function() {
                        if (window.addthis) {
                            window.addthis.init();
                            app.events.off('globalRouter:route', init_addthis);
                        }

                    app.events.on('globalRouter:route', init_addthis);

  <script>
   page.add_feature({
                require: ['AnalyticsHelper'],
                callback: function (app, AnalyticsHelper) {
                    var lazy_analytics = function () {
                        var user,
                            dimensions;

                        if (!analytics.identify) {
                            setTimeout(function () {
                                app.events.trigger('InitializeAnalytics');
                            }, 200);
                            return;
                        }

                        

                        
                            user = null;
                        

                        app.runtime.analytics_helper = new AnalyticsHelper({
                            app: app,
                            user: user,
                            dimensions: dimensions,
                            dimensions_map:  {} ,
                            analytics: analytics
                        });
                        app.events.off('InitializeAnalytics', lazy_analytics);
                    };
                    app.events.on('InitializeAnalytics', lazy_analytics);
                }
            });
  </script>
